She stood, smiled and put on a Warriors cap, striding to the stage backed by the loudest applause of the night. Someone put a microphone in front of her and asked her how it felt. That\u2019s when she finally choked up. \u201dIt changes everything,\u201d she said. \u201dIt means everything to me.\u201d Evans became the first woman ever drafted into the NBA 2K League on Tuesday night, going in the fourth round to Warriors Gaming, which is operated by the NBA\u2019s Golden State Warriors. A former college and semipro basketball player, Evans is now the esports league\u2019s first female pro, one of the 126 players who will make between $33,000 to $37,000 per season, plus benefits and team housing. No more sessions as a trainer at Planet Fitness. The Chicago native is heading to the Bay Area. \u201dIt feels surreal,\u201d she said. Evans was one of two women who qualified for the 2K League draft this year through the league\u2019s online combine. The other, Brianna Novin, was not selected but could still sign as a free agent. The NBA runs the league in coordination with 2K game publisher Take-Two Interactive, and it did not have any women for its inaugural season. Prior to last year\u2019s draft, NBA Commissioner Adam Silver called the lack of gender diversity \u201da disappointment for all of us so far.\u201d The league set out to solve that problem by holding focus groups with top women gamers to spot potential barriers. One key problem: Data showed that male players weren\u2019t passing the ball to their female teammates \u2013 something that wasn\u2019t accounted for when the league analyzed players to build the 2018 draft pool. \u201dIt made us put more emphasis on how good a player was when they got the ball in their hands,\u201d said 2K League managing director Brendan Donohue. \u201dThat\u2019s the only part of it they can control.\u201d The league also monitored communication between players more carefully at this year\u2019s combine, removing several players for sexist remarks. That kind of harassment isn\u2019t new to Evans, or women in esports in general. One of the biggest challenges for women is finding teammates for games that rely so heavily on teamwork. Female gamers can try to ignore an offensive, trash-talking opponent \u2013 and there are plenty of those in the 2K community. But just like in real life, you can\u2019t defend a pick-and-roll if your teammates aren\u2019t willing to communicate. Evans has done most of her competitive gaming with a coed team \u2013 right now, five of its 12 players are women \u2013 and that\u2019s helped her thrive as a shot-creating small forward. Her experience when gaming outside that team \u2013 with both teammates and opponents \u2013 hasn\u2019t always been as rosy. \u201dI\u2019ve had sexual remarks put towards me,\u201d she said. \u201dI get told I should be back in the kitchen. \u20182K is not for women,\u2019 I\u2019ve had that. There\u2019s no question about that.\u201d Evans also got loud pushback on social media when she announced last month \u2013 on her 30th birthday, no less \u2013 that she\u2019d qualified for the draft. \u201dThat\u2019s the only time that it\u2019s been discouraging for me,\u201d Evans said. \u201dIn that moment, because it was a great moment for me, and I felt like people ruined it.\u201d Other gamers at Tuesday\u2019s draft were eager to welcome Evans and Novin. \u201dMale, female, dog, cat, frog, I don\u2019t care,\u201d said Alexander Bernstein, a returning player with 76ers Gaming. \u201dIf you\u2019re the best in the world, I feel like you deserve to be able to play.\u201d That doesn\u2019t mean the women won\u2019t face extra skepticism. Kimanni Ingram, another draft-eligible player, has played with Evans and respects the way she has navigated blowback from male gamers. But even his compliments Tuesday came with a qualifier. \u201dShe has the basketball IQ for a girl,\u201d Ingram said. \u201dMost people would be like, \u2018I\u2019m playing with a girl. She\u2019s not going to know what to do.\u2019 She knows what she\u2019s doing. You can tell.\u201d News of Evans\u2019 selection traveled fast. Warriors coach Steve Kerr was asked about her prior to a game against Boston. \u201dI think that\u2019s really cool that she\u2019s passionate and inspired and broke a barrier,\u201d Kerr said. \u201dThat\u2019s awesome.\u201d \u201dEsports has become a huge thing now,\u201d said Kevin Durant, Evans\u2019 favorite player. \u201dMore people who enjoy the game might get an opportunity to be professionals and make some money for themselves and make some money. I think it\u2019s cool.\u201d Female gamers have had difficulty breaking into pro esports. Among the most popular circuits, League of Legends Championship Series and the Overwatch League have each had just one female player. Those women both received ample praise and criticism on social media. The NBA wants to help Evans and Novin manage that. The 2K League has a transition program based on the NBA\u2019s rookie symposium, and it added sessions specifically for Evans and Novin to help them navigate their potential barrier-breaking roles, including help with social media. One item 2K hopes to change soon: The video game still does not include any female players. Unlike EA Sports\u2019 NBA Live series \u2013 which includes WNBA rosters and the ability to create female players \u2013 NBA 2K is still male-only. Donohue says 2K is working to add women to future versions of the game. That\u2019s not bumming out Evans right now. She\u2019s already building out her to-do list for her new home in Oakland. \u201dI\u2019m going to see if I can do a real-life shooting competition with (Stephen) Curry,\u201d Evans said. \u201dThat\u2019s what I was known for. When LeBron James chose Los Angeles as the place to re-root his family and build his side hustle in entertainment and yes, contend for NBA championships, he never bothered to explain why he chose one L.A. team over the other. And most likely, you never bothered to wonder. You knew. Such is life here, where the blue sky is repainted purple and gold, where the basketball statues out front of Staples Center all share the same uniform, where the track record for success and rich hoops history leans too far in the direction of the Lakers, crushing the Clippers in the process. When the season began, the Clippers merely moved forward once again in the shadows of the nearby circus, far under radar and beyond the glare, sharing the same arena as the Lakers but not the same platform. This is why today feels so \u2026 what\u2019s the word \u2026 gratifying? \u2026 for the L.A. Team Not Fit For A King. The Clippers are actually doing this, aren\u2019t they? They\u2019re about to keep the Lakers and LeBron from making the playoffs. The teams played Monday in what became the unofficial sign-off for the Laker season after the Clippers grabbed a shovel and buried the body, 113-105 , at Staples. Not only did the Lakers deal with boos from the home crowd, but they played without Brandon Ingram and his bum shoulder and then lost Kyle Kuzma with six minutes left to an ankle sprain. The Clippers\u2019 resident pit bull, Patrick Beverley, stayed chippy from the tip to set the tone for his teammates, giving away four inches and 75 pounds while checking LeBron, yet keeping that same intensity to the buzzer. By then, half the crowd was beating traffic. With 18 games left, a 5 1\/2-game deficit for the West\u2019s final playoff position and losses in seven of their last nine, the Lakers have checked out and packed up. And oh, it\u2019ll get even sweeter for the Clippers if they have a better summer than the Lakers, too, when it will be Jerry West vs. Magic Johnson. Suddenly, any and all is possible, because these are not your Donald Sterling Clippers. Based on three-fourths of a season\u2019s worth of evidence, you wonder if and when these will ever be your Jerry Buss Lakers. \u201cI knew coming into this year it would be different from the previous year,\u201d said James, almost resigned to watching the playoffs from home. A decade ago, if you knew a team in L.A. had a coach on the hot seat, a star player feeling beleaguered, suffered from a string of embarrassing losses and was cloaked in controversy, there would be no question which L.A. team that was. But welcome to the 2018-19 season, where there\u2019s been a twist of fate and the Clippers are frisky, free and staring at an upcoming offseason that might become a launching point for the franchise. They don\u2019t have LeBron, and yet they also don\u2019t have the LeBron-created climate that has the Lakers on edge. They are in serious jeopardy of missing the playoffs, which seemed unlikely when James brought his talents to L.A. last summer. That decision supposedly signaled a new renaissance for the team with 16 championships and continued a parade of superstars to play for the Lakers, which started with West and Elgin Baylor some 60 years ago. Life comes at you fast, and LeBron found himself dealing with distracted teammates he tried to send to New Orleans in a failed coup for Anthony Davis and a coach in Luke Walton he doesn\u2019t appear to enthusiastically endorse, along with a first season with the Lakers that\u2019s going up in smoke. \u201cWe didn\u2019t take care of business tonight,\u201d James said. \u201cBut you keep playing to the end and see what happens. At the end of the year, the chips will fall where they may. We\u2019re in a results league. You take the good with the bad and keep pushing forward.\u201d Missing the playoffs will be an ego blow for the Lakers, and for LeBron, his first non-playoff season since 2004-05. The Lakers wouldn\u2019t be in this position had LeBron not missed 18 games with a groin pull, and this team has never been fully healthy since Thanksgiving. Yet that doesn\u2019t forgive losses to the Knicks, Grizzlies, Suns, Hawks and others. It would come as doubly depressing should the Lakers sit home this spring while L.A. throws its support behind the Clippers in the postseason, especially since the Clippers were all but left for dead \u2014 and tanking \u2014 after trading Tobias Harris to the Sixers weeks ago. But the Clippers, unlike the Lakers, play hard for their coach and are 7-3 since the trade. As for tanking, Clippers coach Doc Rivers said the locker room never gave that any serious thought. \u201cThat was never going to happen,\u201d he said. \u201cWe may have lost (games) but we weren\u2019t going to tank. I think people didn\u2019t believe we couldn\u2019t do it even if we wanted to. That talk helped us, because that was a challenge. This is a group that takes pretty well to challenges.\u201d The Clippers weren\u2019t on LeBron\u2019s radar last summer, but maybe their free-agent judgment day is coming. They\u2019re positioned to take advantage of the market without sacrificing their core, making it tough for an A-list free agent to say no. They\u2019ve got a secure coach in Rivers who constantly ranks high in player popularity polls. They have a good supporting cast, all on team-friendly deals: Lou Williams, Montrezl Harrell, Landry Shamet, Shai Gilgeous-Alexander and Beverley. If the Clippers were to find a taker for Danilo Gallinari\u2019s contract, it could create room for two max free agents. Also, they have an owner worth billions in Steve Ballmer who wants to crank up the noise, so neither money nor the luxury tax will be an issue. Finally, the Clippers can offer a free agent all the charms of L.A. without dealing with any of the runoff that often comes with being LeBron\u2019s teammate. You don\u2019t even need to examine his history closely to know that West, now an adviser for the Clippers, usually gets his man. And this summer will be an interesting backroom competition between \u201cThe Logo\u201d and \u201cMagic.\u201d The latter will be under pressure to fix the Lakers, given this season\u2019s collapse and also the three years left on LeBron\u2019s contract. This raises an important question for the Lakers: How will perspective free agents view the idea of playing next to LeBron? It won\u2019t matter in the event of a trade for Davis, who must go wherever the Pelicans send him. But a free agent? It\u2019s best not to suddenly diminish the Lakers on that front, because this franchise remains a destination \u2014 especially if they have money to spend (which they will). Free agents won\u2019t care about how the Lakers stumbled the year before. In this situation, money talks first and foremost. Just the same, placing too much emphasis on this season and projecting something deadly similar for the Lakers next season \u2014 assuming of course, good health for LeBron \u2014 is done at your own risk. But that\u2019s in the distance. For now, the Lakers are the No. 2 team in town, and all that\u2019s left is to observe LeBron\u2019s body language for signs of surrender as he plays out the meaningless string. LeBron gave no definitive answer about how much, if any, he\u2019ll play once the Lakers\u2019 demise is official. \u201cI\u2019ll continue being a professional and great as I can be every single night no matter the circumstances,\u201d he said. Meanwhile, the other team in L.A. is fully activated, to borrow a LeBron term, for the next step. \u201cThere were seven people here to see us media day,\u201d said Beverley. \u201cI remember like it was yesterday. Like I said then, we\u2019re the best team in L.A. A lot of people didn\u2019t believe me. Probably still don\u2019t.\u201d He smirked. \u201cThat\u2019s fine. That\u2019s who we do it for, the people in the back. The blue collar people who don\u2019t have anything given to them. Who work for everything they deserve. "},{"id":35189,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/about-last-night-03-04-2019","date":"2019-03-05","title":"About Last Night: Rising Suns","content":" It was little more than a week ago that the lowly Phoenix Suns found themselves floundering through the worst stretch in team history, an 18-game losing streak in which they absorbed defeats of (among others) 34, 27, 37, 28 and 27 points. The Suns snapped that skid on Feb. 25 , then added their second victory in three outings with an upset of the Lakers last Saturday . So the question entering Monday\u2019s seemingly unwinnable home game against the NBA-best Bucks was obvious: Why stop there? Pulling off one of the league\u2019s most improbable upsets in decades, the Suns somehow prevailed 114-105 , erasing a 16-point deficit in the first half and finishing strong with a combination of effort and execution they\u2019ve lacked so often during yet another lost season. In doing so, the Suns \u2014 who trailed Milwaukee by 36 games in the loss column entering Monday\u2019s action, and 35 1\/2 games overall \u2014 became the first team to beat the Bucks more than once this season, while the Bucks suffered back-to-back defeats for the first time. Even more notably, it marked the first time since 1983-84, when the Indiana Pacers upset the eventual-champion Boston Celtics, that the NBA\u2019s worst team has beaten the NBA\u2019s best team more than 60 games into the season. (For reference, only one current Sun, 38-year-old Jamal Crawford, was alive at that point.) Despite a nip-and-tuck third quarter, in which the lead changed hands six times, the Bucks finally appeared to have things under control as they built up a 10-point lead midway through the fourth. But despite having nothing to play for but pride, the Suns slugged back with a 31-12 surge over the final 7:37. Kelly Oubre was the unlikely star, scoring 27 points, pulling down 13 rebounds and making a critical late defensive play, stripping the ball off Bucks center Brooks Lopez and out of bounds as the Suns defended a four-point lead with 31.5 seconds left. \u201cIt\u2019s kind of hard to think we lost to Phoenix twice,\u201d said the shell-shocked Giannis Antetokounmpo, who was limited to 21 points. \u201cBut they played better than us. They came out there and set the tone.\u201d Making the victory even sweeter, it followed a report from ESPN posted earlier in the day detailing the franchise\u2019s descent into dysfunction with nine straight playoff absences. It will take an exhaustive effort to reverse that decay. But for one game at least, things felt a little brighter in the Valley of the Sun. The Bucks weren\u2019t the only playoff team to blow a big lead to a team playing out the string. They were joined by the Jazz, who were powerless to prevent the visiting Pelicans from erasing a 17-point deficit en route to a 115-112 victory . While plays like this from Anthony Davis certainly helped \u2026 \u2026 the Pelicans largely did it without their presumably soon-to-be-departed superstar. Indeed, for the fifth time in the past six games, they were actually better without him when it mattered most. Maybe life in the Big Easy won\u2019t be so bleak without Davis? As has been the case throughout his final season, Heat legend Dwyane Wade exchanged jerseys with an appreciative opponent. As strange as this one might have seemed, however, it was actually one of the coolest yet. We\u2019ll let D-Wade explain: If there have been two constants during the Gregg Popovich era in San Antonio, they are winning and defense. While the Spurs are still doing the former, the latter has suffered a precipitous drop off as they\u2019re on pace to finish below league average in defensive efficiency for the first time since 1996-97 \u2014 Popovich\u2019s first season at the helm, and the last time they failed to make the postseason. The NBA announced Monday night that the Raptors and Rockets will play on Oct. 8 and Oct. 10 at the Saitama Super Arena. The NBA played 12 regular-season games in Japan between 1990 and 2003. These preseason matchups will be the first time the league has returned to Japan since. \u201cBringing NBA preseason games to Japan will help accelerate the growth of basketball in a country that features a thriving sports culture and one of the world\u2019s largest economies,\u201d NBA Commissioner Adam Silver said. The preseason games will come about nine months before the start of the 2020 Tokyo Olympics. There are pro leagues in Japan, and the nation is one of the 32 teams that will appear in the FIBA World Cup in China this summer. \u201cYou have only to look at our organization to know that we truly believe basketball is a global game,\u201d Raptors President Masai Ujiri said. \u201cWe come from all over the world, and we are all connected through the love of our sport. We are looking forward to sharing that with basketball fans in Japan.\u201d There have been two Japanese-born players in the NBA. Yuta Tabuse played in four games for Phoenix in 2004-05, and Yuta Watanabe has appeared in 10 games with Memphis this season. Houston played two games in Japan in 1992. \u201cOur organization has a great appreciation for our global fan base, and we enthusiastically embrace the NBA\u2019s efforts to grow the game internationally,\u201d Rockets CEO Tad Brown said. Its record went to 41-22, no small feat considering All-Star guard Victor Oladipo\u2019s season ended on Jan. 23 with a ruptured right quadriceps tendon. The Pacers, without their best player, had beaten a bunch of contenders \u2014 Boston, Philadelphia, Houston, Oklahoma City\u2013 to 40 victories and still were going. So as the two men left the building \u2014 Pritchard, 51, Indiana\u2019s president of basketball operations and Walsh, 78, the lifer now serving as a consultant \u2014 Walsh turned to Pritchard and said, \u201cWell, Kevin, you\u2019re not going to have a losing season.\u201d That\u2019s pretty much the Pacers\u2019 way. No sweeping pronouncements about the season, no predictions of playoff success. Just a snapshot of the moment, simple math in a one-day-at-a-time approach. For the rest of us, it\u2019s entirely legitimate to assess Indiana\u2019s 2018-19 season overall, to respect the Pacers\u2019 consistency and to marvel at their ability to absorb the blow of Oladipo\u2019s loss and keep going. Pritchard, the native of Bloomington, Ind., nearing the second anniversary of when he took over for Larry Bird in the team\u2019s basketball hierarchy, spoke recently with Steve Aschburner of NBA.com about another overachieving season.  * * * Steve Aschburner:  I\u2019m not sure whether you guys are the Little Engine That Could or Monty Python\u2019s Black Knight , but what\u2019s the key to your resiliency? Kevin Pritchard:  I really think it starts with what we\u2019re about. Our guys, on a consistent basis, do a couple things: they play hard and they play together. That\u2019s really a testament to [coach] Nate [McMillan] and our coaching staff. Every night, I feel like we give ourselves a chance. We may be not the most talented team, but we try to make up for it by doing the small things well. They\u2019re a competitive group. They believe in each other, and I think they believe in playing the right way. There haven\u2019t been but a handful of games this year where I thought, \u201cMan, we didn\u2019t play super-hard tonight.\u201d SA:  No offense, but the Pacers \u2014 in this era of multi-star Super Teams \u2014 aren\u2019t very \u201csexy.\u201d Is there room for a serious contender going about its business like this? KP:  What we evaluate is, when we look at players, we look at what we\u2019re about. We have some things we feel very strongly about in our culture, and that kind of drives every decision. Sometimes that maybe knocks out the \u201csexy\u201d pick, but it makes us take a hard look at what fits. Our players have done a great job also of establishing what they\u2019re about and holding the locker room accountable. SA:  So the Pacers sometimes get to do the choosing, rather than always hoping to be chosen, by a talented free agent? KP:  I don\u2019t think it comes down to turning down anybody. I think we know what we are in Indianapolis. That doesn\u2019t mean we won\u2019t go after the big names, but when we do our evaluations, we ask ourselves a few questions and if they don\u2019t fit, we mark that. \u201cOK, let\u2019s evaluate the rest of the talent pool.\u201d I\u2019m not sure it\u2019s the right way, but it\u2019s the way we do it. SA:  In games Oladipo was hurt last season, your team was 0-7. As we speak this season, you\u2019re 16-11. What\u2019s the difference, as far as dependency? KP:  We overachieved overall last year. We made a pretty big trade [ Paul George for Oladipo and Domantas Sabonis ] and it worked out for both teams, and that made my job easier coming into this season because we wanted to keep some continuity. Continuity has allowed those guys to get comfortable with each other and gain some confidence. After we had a few wins without Victor, they had a better sense they could win if they played the right way. SA:  You lost your first four after his injury in January, then won nine of the next 12. KP: That\u2019s a real credit to Nate McMillan. You think about juggling as many lineups and dealing with as many changes as we\u2019ve had the last few years, he has done a great job of maximizing the talent. Our staff has great cohesion and this is a tribute to the job they\u2019ve done. SA: Nate\u2019s getting mentioned as a Coach of the Year candidate. Why is he good at his job? KP: Just the consistency. He prepares. He brings the same work ethic every single day and that trickles down to the team. He sees the game in a way he wants it to be played. When it\u2019s not played that way, he lets them know. And I think Nate has had a little bit of a rebirth with his third team now. He\u2019s able to make adjustments. SA: According to some analytics I\u2019ve seen, some of your most efficient five-man lineups have been ones without Oladipo. How does that work? KP: Yeah, I\u2019m not sure I would subscribe to the theory that we have more better lineups without Victor. My eyes would tell me we\u2019re a lot better team when he plays. SA:  How is Oladipo doing in his rehab? KP:  Great. He has hit the reset button and attacks every single day the best he can. He\u2019s getting shots up sitting down in a chair. Whatever Victor can do, he will do \u2014 times a factor of 10. I spent two days with him down in Miami. During that time, he was texting and calling a lot of our guys. I think he stays in really close contact with our team on a daily basis. SA:  In his absence, have you seen any other individuals step up and take more responsibility? KP:  It feels like Thad [Young] has really stepped up into that captaincy role and become more vocal. We have a leadership group with Darren [Collison] and Bojan and now Wes Matthews, along with Myles Turner and Sabonis, they\u2019ve all stepped in. I\u2019m not sure we have one guy who has a dominant voice \u2014 it feels like this team polices itself in holding everybody accountable. SA:  What was your sales pitch to Matthews? KP:  He saw opportunity, right? We needed a starting two. And there was continuity with just knowing Nate and how he coaches, his style [Matthews and McMillan were together in Portland for 1 1\/2 seasons]. And from what he\u2019s told us, he saw us, he played against us and he liked the way we play. But it became a recruiting process, for sure. He had a lot of options. SA:  The Pacers are at or near the top in a number of defensive metrics, from defensive rating and points allowed per game to opponents\u2019 field goal percentage and sheer fouling . What\u2019s the secret of that success? KP:  Dan Burke is our defensive coach . He should get a lot of credit. And it\u2019s the fabric of what we are. Before we walk out to practice, I can assure you all of our coaches have thought about defense first. It\u2019s their nature, it\u2019s the way we evaluate film, it\u2019s the way we look at players. It\u2019s kind of who we are. SA:  So how has this gone for you in Year 2 in your current role?  KP:  I think this is my ninth year here. It seems short but it\u2019s been a while. I work with Donnie Walsh and Larry Bird [advisor to the Pacers president] on a daily basis, and both guys are true mentors for me. Donnie\u2019s in the office every day. Larry\u2019s here in the fall, then he\u2019s back for the Draft and free agency \u2014 he\u2019s very involved. I think he really enjoys this team. SA:  OK, but what have you learned about the job and the business? For instance, you deftly navigated a situation that has gotten a lot of league attention lately \u2014 the star player who wants out. I know you called it a trade that worked out for both teams, but the challenge initially was to move Paul George without taking a serious step back . KP:  I think the biggest thing is, you\u2019ve got to get in a room with your staff and your coaching staff, and have a good, hard debate about everything you do. You have to board out the noise and try to do what\u2019s right. SA:  There\u2019s a lot more noise as you call it than there used to be. It\u2019s unfathomable now, for example, that Kareem Abul-Jabbar could have asked for a trade back in 1974 and his boss in Milwaukee, Wayne Embry, could keep it quiet for a whole season. KP:  Oh my gosh, [the noise is] almost infinite now. You can almost guarantee tomorrow that there\u2019s going to be more [off-court] stories.  SA:  What\u2019s your assessment of the group you added last summer : Tyreke Evans, Doug McDermott and Kyle O\u2019Quinn? KP:  They fit in nicely. They all made it clear that they wanted to come in, play a role and do it as well as they possibly could. Kyle is a great backup center, and we\u2019ve asked him to be the third center. We\u2019ve needed him, because Sabonis is going to be out for a little bit. McDermott, as he gets comfortable here and learns to seek out his offense, the better he\u2019s going to be. And Tyreke, he\u2019s had some ups and downs. But when he plays well, we\u2019re a different team. We need that punch off the bench, and that\u2019s something we focused on when he got him. SA:  How do you know from night to night whether he\u2019s going to provide that? KP:  I can\u2019t tell that for the whole team. You just never know. SA:  [TJ] Leaf had a big game against Minnesota Thursday [18 points]. He was the No. 18 pick in 2017 [ahead of prospects such as Brooklyn\u2019s Jarrett Allen, Toronto\u2019s OG Anunoby and the Lakers\u2019 Kyle Kuzma and Josh Hart]. Do you still see in him the player you projected? KP:  We\u2019re really high on him. He has paid his dues. He got stronger last year. The physicality of the game was a little bit of a challenge \u2014 that\u2019s not his challenge anymore. He\u2019s got a real offensive feel. He\u2019s one of our best in the post. He has a patience about him. He can go either way \u2014 he can pass. We think he\u2019s got a shot to be a really nice NBA player because he just works so hard. The game is slowing down for him. SA:  Bogdanovic got a lot of attention on the Timberwolves broadcast as a player who could help a bunch of teams. With six or seven of your top 10 heading into free agency , what impact is that having on your immediate and longer-term futures? KP:  It\u2019s good in that guys are pretty motivated. I\u2019ve believed in this team. We\u2019re going to be challenged in the playoffs and it will be fun watching them, but we\u2019ve got to get there first. I don\u2019t want to look too far in the future. We know we\u2019re going to have some tough decisions this summer. But I believe 40 percent of the league will be free agents, so it\u2019s not only our issue. It\u2019s a league issue and an opportunity. SA:  Did your fan base need to be persuaded, after Oladipo went down, not to bail on this season? Or did they remember how plucky the Pacers were in nearly upsetting Cleveland last spring and sign on for more of the same? KP:  That\u2019s a good question. We\u2019ve had great fans the last two years. We\u2019ve been a tough out at home. And our fan base is educated. They know basketball, and I think they respect when they see a team play hard, whether it\u2019s a win or a loss. You can\u2019t fool \u2018em. And we don\u2019t try to fool anybody. SA:  We haven\u2019t seen Indiana opt for the \u201crace to the bottom\u201d approach to team building. KP:  You\u2019ve got to give Herb [Simon, team owner] a ton of credit. He\u2019s not the kind of guy who says, \u201cLet\u2019s tank and look to the future in three years.\u201d We\u2019re not about that. SA:  This is such a bottom-line business. But considering everything that\u2019s happened already, can you take satisfaction now in what your team has accomplished? Or does it necessarily have to wait until the end, with so much determined by your last game? KP:  I\u2019d rather you ask me at the end of the year. I know we\u2019re not going to have a losing season, though. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. You can e-mail him here , find his archive here and follow him on Twitter . The victory they earned on Monday not only kept the Pistons perfect since the All-Star break, but was a win against a top-seeded squad they could face come the actual postseason. Raptors 118, Celtics 95 \u2014 The Raptors entered Tuesday\u2019s showdown needing a win to tie the season series with the Celtics. In the process, they sent a decided message to a fellow East favorite, too. Pascal Siakam and Kyle Lowry got the starters rolling, while Marc Gasol came through with some critical points off the bench to fuel a blowout victory. Nuggets 121, Thunder 112 \u2014 This is the time of year when division matchups matter most. Thanks to Nikola Jokic, Denver once again proved its might in the Northwest Division chase. Denver improved to 3-0 against OKC to clinch the season series as well as build a four-game lead in the division chase. Hawks 131, Wolves 123 \u2014 Atlanta, in the opinion of many, has little to no reason to aim for success this season. Don\u2019t tell that to youngsters Trae Young and John Collins, though. They both put up 30-point games on Wednesday, serving to both spoil some of Minnesota\u2019s playoff hopes and also provide a look at a potentially bright combination in the Hawks\u2019 future. Heat 126, Warriors 125 \u2014 It had been more than two months since Dwyane Wade went bananas from 3-point range in a win. Fittingly, he did so against the defending champions on Wednesday night, with 3-pointer No. 5 coming in the most astounding way possible. His one-legged, off-the-glass, straightaway 3-point heave dropped the Warriors in what might have been the best shot of 2018-19. Bucks 141, Kings 140 (OT) \u2014 Milwaukee is a team that is much more than Kia MVP candidate Giannis Antetokounmpo, and it proved that in spades against Sacramento. With Antetokounmpo resting under a minutes restriction and fellow All-Star Khris Middleton hobbled, guards Eric Bledsoe and Malcolm Brogdon saved the day in a thrilling win vs. the Kings. Rockets 121, Heat 118 \u2014 Three days after his 30-point scoring streak ended, James Harden got his newest such streak to two in grand fashion. He dropped 58 points and 10 assists on the Heat in a comeback win, the seventh such game in his storied career. He nailed eight 3-pointers and overall was unstoppable no matter who guarded him on Thursday night. Sixers 108, Thunder 104 \u2014 Before this one began on Thursday, it seemed like somewhat of an even game based on who wouldn\u2019t be playing (Paul George and Joel Embiid). No one told that to Tobias Harris, who put the Sixers on his back with 32 points and several clutch buckets late in the fourth quarter to help Philly to its first-ever win in Oklahoma City. Bulls 168, Hawks 161 (4 OT) \u2014 Don\u2019t tell Atlanta and Chicago they\u2019re only playing for Draft lottery positioning. Given the effort and scoring performances from both teams on Friday, it looked like much more was on the line for both squads. Trae Young set a Hawks rookie record with 49 points, making 17 of 33 shots (including six 3-pointers). Not to be outdone, the Bulls\u2019 Zach LaVine had a career-high 47 on 17-for-35 shooting with six 3-pointers. Raptors 119, Blazers 117 \u2014 Last week, Kawhi Leonard came up with a big steal and bucket, clinching a Raptors\u2019 win against San Antonio (and on DeMar DeRozan\u2019s return night). This week, Leonard was up to those tricks again, this time vanquishing Portland with a game-winning bucket with 1.5 seconds left on Friday night. Warriors 120, Sixers 117 \u2014 Don\u2019t ever sleep on Stephen Curry. That was a valuable lesson Philly learned on Saturday, as it watched its fourth-quarter lead fizzle and fade thanks to Curry\u2019s exploits. After a mostly quiet game, the Warriors\u2019 star scored 11 of his 28 points in the final frame \u2014 including a critical 3-pointer \u2014 that sank the Sixers\u2019 hopes of scoring an upset win. Jazz 115, Bucks 111 \u2014 A Kia MVP contender doing all he can to preserve a win. A young superstar (and, perhaps, future Kia MVP type) refusing to let up. And one of the best finishes of 2018-19, too. This Saturday night showdown had it all from Salt Lake City, with Giannis Antetokounmpo going for 43 points \u2014 only to be bested by the Jazz\u2019s Donovan Mitchell dropping 46 points to lift the Jazz from a 17-point, fourth-quarter hole. Abdul-Jabbar, 71, put up 234 items, including four of his six championship rings, for auction, with most of the proceeds targeted for his Skyhook Foundation that sends children from economically-challenged backgrounds to summer camps focusing on science, technology and engineering. Per ESPN\u2019s report, Abdul-Jabbar\u2019s 1986-87 championship ring with the Los Angeles Lakers drew the highest price of any item at $398,937.50. In addition, Abdul-Jabbar\u2019s other rings from the Lakers\u2019 1980s title runs accounted for four of the five highest sales at the auction\u2019s close. His 1985 championship ring sold for $343,700 while his \u201980 and \u201988 rings went for $245,000 each. The ball from the final NBA regular-season game he played in back in 1989 sold for $270,050. Three of Abdul-Jabbar\u2019s six MVP trophies \u2014 from \u201972, \u201974 and \u201976 \u2014 each sold for more than $120,000.  \u201cWhen it comes to choosing between storing a championship ring or trophy in a room, or providing kids with an opportunity to change their lives, the choice is pretty simple: Sell it all,\u201d said Abdul-Jabbar, in a statement explaining his aim. \u201cLooking back on what I have done with my life, instead of gazing at the sparkle of jewels or gold plating celebrating something I did a long time ago, I\u2019d rather look into the delighted face of a child holding their first caterpillar and think about what I might be doing for their future. That\u2019s a history that has no price.\u201d In addition to various items from his NBA playing days, Abdul-Jabbar was also auctioning off his class ring from Power Memorial High School, a pair of his iconic (game-worn) goggles, an ice bucket, a portrait of Abraham Lincoln, a VHS recording of his Hall of Fame induction in 1995 and various other awards from his past. Abdul-Jabbar, 71, is the NBA\u2019s all-time leading scorer with 38,387 points. When he left the game in 1989 at age 42, no NBA player had ever scored more points, blocked more shots, won more Most Valuable Player Awards, played in more All-Star Games or logged more seasons. In his storied career, Abdul-Jabbar was Rookie of the Year, a member of six NBA championship teams, a six-time NBA MVP, a two-time NBA Finals MVP, a 19-time All-Star, a two-time scoring champion and a member of the NBA 35th and 50th Anniversary All-Time Teams."},{"id":35232,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/bucks-sign-gasol","date":"2019-03-04","title":"Milwaukee Bucks sign Pau Gasol","content":"MILWAUKEE \u2013 The Milwaukee Bucks have signed center Pau Gasol to a contract. Gasol, who is in his 18th season in the NBA, is a six-time All-Star, four-time All-NBA selection and two-time NBA Champion. He\u2019s appeared in 1,223 games (1,150 starts) throughout his career with Memphis, the Los Angeles Lakers, Chicago and San Antonio and holds career averages of 17.1 points, 9.2 rebounds, 3.2 assists and 1.6 blocks per game. Speaking at the MIT Sloan Sports Analytics Conference on Friday, Silver raised the idea of replacing the All-Star Game with a midseason or preseason tournament in which teams would compete for a separate championship, like they do in European soccer. Or groups of teams could compete in mini-tournaments in Asia or Europe. The problem, Silver said, is how to make these other events meaningful. \u201cThe All-Star Game didn\u2019t work,\u201d he said, calling it \u201can afterthought\u201d of the weekend despite changes like tinkering with the rosters through a player draft that was made public for the first time. \u201cI get it. We put an earring on a pig.\u201d The league is unlikely to make any changes \u2013 at least not any time soon \u2013 if only because a 70-game schedule like the one Silver discussed would require each team to give up six home games. Although players and coaches would love to see a shorter season, none is excited about taking a 20 percent pay cut. But the analytics conference in Boston\u2019s Bay Bay convention center gives Silver the opportunity to think aloud about ways to make the NBA better. In past years he has addressed possible changes to the draft to discourage teams from tanking, but this year\u2019s hot topic was New Orleans Pelicans star Anthony Davis. Silver said Davis\u2019 public trade request (through his agent) was a problem for the league, but not all that different than other players who made the request behind the scenes. The more frequent shuffling of stars among teams was an unintended consequence of a collective bargaining agreement that was designed to shorten contracts so players wouldn\u2019t be earning huge salaries long after they were productive. \u201cMaybe that was a mistake,\u201d Silver said. Davis told the Pelicans he would not accept an extension, but the team did not trade him before the deadline and then mulled whether to sit him out to minimize the risk of injury \u2013 and maximize its draft position. He is expected to be traded over the summer. \u201cIt\u2019s a bad dynamic,\u201d Silver said. \u201cIt\u2019s a bit of a mess.\u201d"},{"id":35230,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/pau-gasol-reportedly-sign-bucks","date":"2019-03-01","title":"Spurs part with Pau Gasol, who'll reportedly sign with Bucks","content":" SAN ANTONIO (AP) \u2014 The San Antonio Spurs announced a buyout agreement with Pau Gasol on Friday, allowing the veteran center to become playoff-eligible with another team. As a defender. \u201cMany times in the huddle, late in games, we\u2019ll say \u2018E, this guy\u2019s got it going on. You\u2019ve got to get him,\u2019 \u201d says Villanova assistant coach Kyle Neptune. \u201cCoach [Jay Wright] always wants Eric to check the other team\u2019s hot hand. It doesn\u2019t even matter what position it is.\u201d Some question whether Paschall \u2014 whose name has been turning up in the first round of some mock NBA Drafts \u2014 can be that effective a defender at the next level. The men who have coached him the last four years, counting a valuable redshirt season after Paschall transferred from Fordham in 2015, scoff at the naysayers. \u201cIt\u2019s preposterous,\u201d Neptune says. \u201cWe\u2019ve had elite defenders here \u2014 Josh Hart, Mikail Bridges \u2026 Donte Divincenzio was a good defender \u2014 but I\u2019d put Eric with any of those guys. The NBA is so much more isolations and making plays. I think Eric would be very good defensively in the NBA, right away. I don\u2019t think there would be any lag time.\u201d La Salle coach Ashley Howard, who served on Wright\u2019s staff as the Wildcats won two national titles, has a more succinct answer when asked if he thinks Paschal can guard at the next level. \u201cAsk Devonte Graham if he can\u2019t guard,\u201d Howard says. Villanova played Kansas in the Final Four last season, and Graham scored 23 points, meaning Wright had to dispatch Paschal to cool him off. The Wildcats eventually won 95-79. Long before he played as a Fordham freshman in 2014, Paschall earned the reputation of a scorer. And he didn\u2019t disappoint. The big man dropped 31 in his first college game, averaged 16 points and was voted the Atlantic 10 Conference Rookie of the Year. But after his coach, Tom Pecora, was fired in March 2015, Paschall decided he didn\u2019t want to stay around. Villanova had called Paschall just days before he signed with Fordham, so it was a natural place to resurface. His choice was astute. From the day he first stepped on campus \u2014 weighing 268 pounds with 18 percent body fat \u2014 Paschall went to work on his body under the watchful eye of John Shackleton, Villanova\u2019s excellent strength and conditioning coach who\u2019s also a nutritionist. Paschall used his redshirt year of 2015-16 wisely. As he watched the Wildcats win their first national title under Wright, he was toning and strengthening his body. By the time he was eligible to play the next season, Paschall was a ripped 251 pounds with six percent body fat. \u201cI give coach Shack a lot of the credit,\u201d Paschall says. \u201cWe lifted every day, he taught me how to eat right, and we worked on all the little things \u2014 lunges, box step ups, drills to help you get good mobility throughout your body.\u201d Paschall was a complimentary player as a sophomore in 2016-17, averaging 7.2 points. He knew there was more work to be done, so in between working with Neptune on his defensive skills, Paschall cranked up perimeter shots by the hundreds. Last season, when the Wildcats won another national title, he was a key starter, averaged 10.6 points and shot 35.6 from beyond the arc and 81.3 from the free-throw line. A year earlier, his averages were 27.9 and 69.5. Paschall derived just as much satisfaction becoming Villanova\u2019s lockdown man. \u201cIt\u2019s fun taking on all [defensive] challenges,\u201d Paschall said. \u201cAgainst quickness, I try to slide and use my length [6-foot-11 wingspan] to keep them in front of me. With big guys, I chest them. I use my strength when they try to back me down and not let them get to the spot where the want to.\u201d The NBA Draft claimed three starters \u2014 Bridges, point guard Jalen Brunson and post Omari Spellman \u2014 and key reserve Divincenzo \u2014 from that national championship team, leaving Paschall and fellow senior Phil Booth to carry on a proud tradition. The Wildcats began this season ranked in everyone\u2019s Top 25, fell out after improbable losses to Furman and Penn \u2014 which broke the Wildcats\u2019 25-game winning streak over Philadelphia Big Five competition \u2014 and have spent the rest of the year battling back. At 21-8 overall and 12-4 in the Big East, Villanova is poised to return to the NCAA tournament, thanks in large part to Booth and Paschall (16.8 ppg, 6.1 rpg, 36.8 from 3-point range). \u201cIt\u2019s been difficult with only two starters back,\u201d Paschall says. \u201cBut when all those guys left [all four of Villanova\u2019s Draft picks had eligibility remaining] we were happy for them. They got to follow their dreams. So Phil and I have had to do all the little things, and take over leadership roles to show the young guys what Villanova basketball is all about.\u201d Lately, Villanova basketball has been about winning championships and sending players to the NBA. Neptune and Howard think Paschall will be next in line. \u201cThe maturation of his career has been impressive to watch,\u201d Neptune says. \u201cHe started as a complete iso guy, just a volume shooter. He transitioned when he got here into more of a role player. You go your whole life, even the first part of college, being the guy, and now you have to learn to operate in a role. That\u2019s not easy. Over his first couple years here he did a great job finding his spots in the offense. \u201cThen he goes back to being the guy after not doing it in a while. It\u2019s another challenge, at the highest level of the game, being at the top of the scouting report. On top of that, when he\u2019s locked in and he\u2019s playing hard, no one in our program\u2019s been a better defender in terms of staying in front of guys. I think he\u2019s a plug-and-play guy in the NBA.\u201d Howard agrees. \u201cI think he\u2019ll be better in the NBA than he is in college because it\u2019s more of an open game,\u201d Howard says. \u201cEric can shoot, he\u2019s an NBA-caliber athlete, and he\u2019s a guy that can defend, legitimately defend, multiple positions. \u201cI haven\u2019t seen everybody in college basketball, but what guy other than [Duke freshman ] Zion Williamson has the size, the athletic skill and the explosiveness Eric does? The Sixers will be without All-Star Joel Embiid, who remains sidelined with left knee soreness. http:\/\/George%20out%20vs.%20Sixers%20with%20right%20shoulder%20soreness"},{"id":35270,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/pat-riley-heat-targeting-summer-2020","date":"2019-02-28","title":"Riley: Heat will be eyeing max free agents in 2020","content":" Miami Heat president Pat Riley is no stranger to building a winning team in South Florida. He did so when he first arrived in 1995, in trading for franchise stalwarts Alonzo Mourning and Tim Hardaway . In 2004, he added an in-his-prime Shaquille O\u2019Neal to a burgeoning star in Dwyane Wade \u2014 a core that won Miami it\u2019s first NBA title in 2006. And he engineered the 2010 \u201cHeatles\u201d squad of Wade, LeBron James and Chris Bosh, all of whom helped Miami to four straight NBA Finals and titles in 2012 and \u201913. In an interview with Heat broadcaster Jason Jackson , Riley says he\u2019s targeting the summer of 2020 as perhaps his next chance to make a big splash with the roster. \u201cWe\u2019ve done this four times now, had a good group of players, young players, and then either through free agency or through trade brought the superstar in,\u201d Riley said . \u201cIn 2020, we\u2019ll have a lot of room. We\u2019ll also have the possibility to have enough room to go after two max contracts. And we\u2019re going to do that. So, we\u2019re planning that 2020 will be the room year. \u201cWe\u2019re very fluid. We\u2019re very on top of it. And we are a destination place, Jax. The tax, the sun, the beautiful city. It\u2019s a very progressive city, diverse city. So, we are a destination place. And we\u2019re going to be moving in that direction.\u201d In the interview, Riley praised the team\u2019s young core players such as Justise Winslow, Derrick Jones Jr., Bam Adebayo, Hassan Whiteside and others. He knows chasing a playoff spot is likely the highest goal the team can hope to attain in Miami\u2019s remaining 22 games. After last night\u2019s stunning win against the Golden State Warriors , the Heat trail the Charlotte Hornets for the No. 8 seed by 1\/2 game . \u201cWe\u2019re chasing a playoff spot when we\u2019re young. And then we\u2019re going to be chasing some players that can come in,\u201d Riley said. \u201cIf we can get one or two players to come in with this group, this young group, then I think the sky\u2019s the limit for this team in the next couple years.\u201d After last season\u2019s first-round playoff exit, Riley had said the Heat would think big roster-wise if the opportunity presented itself. However, the Heat made mostly small moves last summer, chief among them re-signing Wade and fellow franchise icon Udonis Haslem. Wade is in the midst of his farewell season, one Wade termed his \u201cone last dance\u201d season. While the Heat have hovered around the .500 mark all season, Riley says missing out on the playoffs in hope of a better Draft position has never been his goal. \u201cI have never thought of anything else other than we want to be a playoff team. We want to think about the championship,\u201d Riley said. \u201cYou can\u2019t ever give up on make the playoffs. \u2026 I don\u2019t care where you are, you get the right match-up, you get the right player that breaks through, you get the right call \u2014 and you\u2019re on to the next round. I don\u2019t care if you\u2019re fighting for a playoff spot \u2014 the No. 8 or 7 or 5 or 3 or the top spot or you\u2019re fighting for a championship. You\u2019ve got to be chasing something positive.\u201d Information from The Associated Press was used in this report."},{"id":35305,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/one-team-one-stat-nuggets-get-defensive","date":"2019-02-28","title":"One Team, One Stat: Nuggets' defense looking a bit more golden","content":" * Tonight on TNT:  Jazz vs. Nuggets, 10:30 ET After missing the playoffs by the thinnest of margins last season, the Denver Nuggets are doing their best to make sure that there will be no doubt this time around. With 22 games to play, the Nuggets are just four wins from matching last season\u2019s total. After a big victory over the Oklahoma City Thunder on Tuesday, Denver has a five-game winning streak and a four-game edge over OKC for the 2 seed in the Western Conference. And thanks to Dwyane Wade\u2019s miraculous game-winner on Wednesday , the Nuggets are tied in the loss column with the first-place Golden State Warriors. The Nuggets have a tougher remaining schedule than the champs, with 13 of their 22 games against teams that currently have winning records. One of those games is Thursday, ( 10:30 p.m. ET, TNT ), when the Nuggets host the Utah Jazz. Here\u2019s one number to know about the 2018-19 Nuggets as they try to extend their winning streak to six games \u2026 The Nuggets are the only Western Conference team that ranks in the top 10 in both offensive and defensive efficiency.  For the second straight season, the Golden State Warriors have not defended to their standards in the regular season. They have the most efficient offense we\u2019ve ever seen, but rank 16th on defense. The other three teams that rank in the top 10 on both ends are in the Eastern Conference. The Nuggets are barely in the top 10 defense, but that is a big step forward. Entering this season, Denver was one of just two teams \u2014 the Sacramento Kings were the other \u2014 that had ranked in the bottom 10 in defensive efficiency each of the last five seasons. And only three teams have improved more defensively from last season. An improvement of 2.1 points per 100 possessions may not seem that big. But as a whole, the league has scored 109.4 points per 100 possessions this season, up from 107.7 last season. So the Nuggets went from allowing 2.2 more points per 100 possessions than the league average to allowing 1.6 fewer than the league average. Improvement has come in a few different areas. The Nuggets have gone from 26th to 17th in effective field goal percentage, from 11th to fifth in defensive rebounding percentage, and from 22nd to 15th in opponent turnover rate. Shooting is the most important thing on both ends of the floor, so the drop in opponent effective field goal percentage is the biggest key to the step forward the Nuggets have taken. And where the Nuggets have improved the most is in their opponents\u2019 shooting from beyond the arc. The Nuggets (37.8 percent) ranked last in opponent 3-point percentage last season , the third straight year in which they ranked in the bottom four. This season, they rank fifth in opponent 3-point percentage, and no team has seen a bigger improvement. The Nuggets have actually seen one of the league\u2019s biggest increases in the percentage of their opponents\u2019 shots that have come from 3-point range. But there\u2019s a bigger correlation between overall defensive efficiency and opponent 3-point percentage than there is between efficiency and 3-pointers attempted\/field goal attempts. Opponent 3-point percentage can be noisy data. There\u2019s some luck involved and it can be more about the player shooting the 3-pointer than the team defending it. But there are ways that the defensive scheme and effort can make an impact. And the Nuggets\u2019 defense has been able to make more of an impact this season.  According to Second Spectrum tracking, the Nuggets have contested a greater percentage of their opponents 3-point attempts than they did last season. Also, 28 percent of their opponents\u2019 3-point attempts have been off the dribble, up from 25 percent last season. With the league shooting 37 percent on catch-and-shoot 3-pointers and just 33 percent on off-the-dribble threes, forcing more of the latter can made a difference. Denver opponents have taken 29 percent of their 3-point attempts (the league\u2019s highest rate) from the corners, where league-wide 3-point percentage is higher (38.3 percent) than it is from above the break (34.8 percent). They almost lost in Memphis in late January when their pick-and-roll defense allowed Justin Holiday to drain a wide-open, weak-side corner 3-pointer for the lead in the final minute. But the Nuggets rank second in opponent 3-point percentage (32.5 percent) on those above-the break 3-pointers, which still account for more than 70 percent of the total threes that their opponents have taken. The Nuggets\u2019 defense has had its ups and downs this season. They ranked fourth defensively (104.1 points per 100 possessions) over the first nine weeks (through Dec. 16), but then ranked 27th (114.0) over the next eight (Dec. 17 \u2013 Feb. 10). They\u2019ve turned things back around, though, having allowed just 97.7 points per 100 possessions over their five-game winning streak, their best five-game stretch of defense since late November. Health has made a difference. The Nuggets have been without Gary Harris for 25 games this season. Paul Millsap was also out for most of December, when that defensive slide began. The Nuggets have allowed just 102.0 points per 100 possessions in 632 minutes with Harris, Millsap and Nikola Jokic on the floor together, even though most of those minutes have come against the opponents\u2019 starters. Harris is still coming off the bench, but improved health has been a factor in the Nuggets\u2019 five-game winning streak. Their opponents have shot just 43-for-165 (26.1 percent) from 3-point range over the five games, improving the Nuggets to 28-5 when their opponent has shot worse than the league average (35.4 percent) from 3-point range. They\u2019re 23-0 when their opponent has made less than 30 percent of its 3-pointers, something that happened just 13 times all of last season . The Nuggets\u2019 improved 3-point defense has shown up most in big moments. They\u2019re a league-best 24-10 in games that were within five points in the last five minutes , in part because they\u2019ve allowed the fewest points per 100 possessions (95.6) with the score within five points in the last five minutes of the fourth quarter or overtime . Their opponents have shot just 15-for-70 (21 percent \u2013 the league\u2019s second lowest opponent mark) on clutch 3-pointers (that Holiday three noted above was the exception to the rule, apparently). The winning streak (which includes two clutch wins) has pushed the Nuggets back into the top 10 in defensive efficiency, a benchmark for teams hoping to make noise in the postseason. Of the 44 teams to reach The Finals in the 23 seasons for which we have play-by-play data\u2026 It\u2019s been 10 years since the Nuggets won a playoff series and six years since they made the postseason. They\u2019re still a few steps away (with the Warriors\u2019 dynasty being a major road block) from even thinking about The Finals. But climbing from the bottom 10 to the top 10 on defense is a step already taken.
